# Break of Dawn
A new TTRPG set in the world of Bungie and 343 Industries’ HALO franchise, made by Benjamin Vick and edited by Charles Lesser, Ethan Crowley,  Alec Sabbe, and John Thoma

### Tactical Guide  
A guide to all that you need to know to play the Break of Dawn along with weapons, enemies and allies indexes.

# Rules
## Basic Rules and Operations

What is Break of Dawn?  
Break of Dawn is a tabletop roleplaying game based on the Halo franchise set anytime during, preceding, or succeeding the main storyline. You and your fireteam of Spartans, each with a unique skill set, is tasked with carrying out missions necessary to the survival of Earth and her colonies. You may find yourself allying with the Arbiter and his Swords of Sanghelios to infiltrate a Covenant war base, assassinating a high-profile Banished target, or even fighting off hordes of flood-infected marines. The actions taken by you and your fireteam may very well decide the fate of humanity and change the course of history. Good luck soldier, and remember, Spartans never die.

![[Classes]]
   

Dice, DC, and Other Abbreviated Terms  
Throughout this Tactical Guide, there will be many instances where dice will need to be rolled to determine damage, a certain outcome, or other variable circumstances. Standard dice sets have 2-sided, 4-sided, 6-sided, 8-sided, 12-sided, 20-sided, and 100-sided dice that are used in various situations. For simplicity, this Tactical Guide refers to dice in relation to how many sides they have. For example, a d100 is a 100-sided dice, a d20 is a 20-sided dice, a d12 is a 12-sided dice, etc.  
Additionally, many weapons, abilities, and other aspects of the game refer to what is known as a “DC.” This is an abbreviation for “Difficulty Class” and designates the number you must roll to succeed on an interaction, attack, or other action. Unless otherwise stated, a roll equal to or exceeding the DC number is considered a success, while one rolled below the DC is considered a failure.

Rules of Engagement  
	A Spartan is a living weapon; a human being modified and trained to the very pinnacle of martial capability for the sole purpose of defending humanity across a myriad of frontiers. As such, the first and foremost duty of a Spartan is to be a shield between the human race and those who would do them harm, making Combat the mainstay of the Spartan experience. *Break of Dawn* reflects this by centering the game around Combat and Warfare, as well as other elements such as exploration, investigation, and even social interaction that may serve as facets of the multifarious missions Spartans find themselves dispatched on. 

The Basics of Combat: Turns, Operations, and Combat Time  
When considering a battle between a Spartan Fireteam and their foes, it is crucial to understand what is happening and when. What may be several minutes of planning and discussion to the players may be but a split-second to the Spartans they control. As such, Combat in *Break of Dawn* is divided into *Rounds*, which are themselves composed of a number of *Turns*, which are themselves further subdivided into units called *Operations*.  
 Each *round* of combat represents 6 seconds of real time. In-game, a round of combat lasts until all creatures involved in that combat have taken a *turn*. A new round begins from the top of the initiative order after the last creature has taken their turn. On an individual turn, a creature takes a number of *Operations*, representing the different actions and feats of derring-do they can perform on their turn. On a single turn, a creature may take one *Primary* Operation, one *Secondary* Operation, and one *Tertiary* Operation, each one representing a split-second action or reaction undertaken in the heat of battle.   
The order in which creatures’ turns progress in a given round of combat is determined at the very beginning of the combat encounter by rolling for *Initiative*.

Initiative  
At the beginning of combat, all creatures involved in the combat will roll a d100 adding their dodge bonus. The creature with the highest total takes the first turn in each round of combat, followed by the second highest, third highest, and so on until all creatures have taken a turn and the next round of combat, where the turn order begins again from the creature with the highest total. If two or more creatures tie when rolling for initiative, the creature with the higher base roll, excluding bonuses, goes first. If there is still a tie, the creatures must each roll another d100 without any bonuses to determine who goes first, with the highest roll winning the tie.

Taking a Primary Operation  
Primary Operations are the main actions you do on your turn. During your turn in combat, there are many different options that you can choose. The Operations you can take are:

**Attack:**   
Use your Primary Operation to make an attack against a creature within range of the weapon. You can attack up to as many times as your current weapon allows.

**Use an Item:**  
Some items require a Primary Operation to use. You can expend a Primary Operation to immediately gain the effect of one such item that you possess. 

**Revive:**  
Use your Primary Operation to stabilize an unconscious ally; they regain 10 health and are exposed to the Wounded effect.

**Grenade:**  
Use your Primary Operation to make an attack with a grenade at a specified target. You may only do this if you have access to grenades. 

**Punch:**   
As a Primary Operation, a creature may make a punch attack against a target within 5 feet. The target must succeed on a dodge DC 65 or take 21 (6d6) kinetic damage. If the target succeeds the dodge, they take no damage.

Secondary Operations  
Some abilities are triggered in a Secondary Operation. On a creature’s turn, they may take one Secondary Operation before or after other types of Operations. It does not count as your Primary Operation, meaning that a creature can take a Secondary Operation and Primary Operation in the same turn.

**Reload:**  
A creature can use a Secondary Operation to reload their weapon after rolling a 1 on an Ammo Die (explained further in the Weapon Statistics section).

Tertiary Operations  
A Tertiary Operation is the smallest Operation a creature can take on its turn. Like a Secondary Operation, a creature may make one Tertiary Operation before or after any other Operations on its turn, and can be used alongside both Primary and Secondary Operations.

**Change Weapons:**   
A creature can use a Tertiary Operation to switch to another weapon in their possession. When they switch to a weapon, they may only make attacks with that weapon until they expend a Tertiary Operation to switch to a new weapon on another turn. 

**Interact:**  
Use a Tertiary Operation to interact with or activate a certain object within your reach, such as a door, console, lever, dropped weapon, etc. 

Reactive Operations  
Certain abilities are used as Reactive Operations. These are special Operations that a creature takes as a result of an external trigger or event at no cost to the creature’s other Operations. Depending on the trigger, a creature may be able to use Reactive Operations even when it is not its turn. Abilities that cost Reactive Operations will specify that they cost Reactive Operations as well as their trigger. 

Other Operations  
At the GM’s discretion, any other actions not listed above could be designated as certain Operations. 

Attacking, Dodging, Damage, and Injury  
Ultimately, the goal of combat will be either to sufficiently injure your opponent so that they are no longer a threat to you, or to prevent them from doing so to you. By taking the *Attack* Primary Operation, a creature makes an attack with the weapon they are currently armed with against a target creature (or target creatures, dependent on the nature of the attack and the weapon used), who must then attempt to avoid the attack (by dodging) or suffer injury (damage) from it, reducing the target creature’s Health by a certain amount (see **Health**, **Damage Types**, and **Death**, below)

Health  
Health represents the amount of physical trauma a creature or vehicle can sustain without dying or being destroyed. When a creature or vehicle takes damage, they lose health. The only ways to recover lost health are through downtime (see **Downtime**) or through using a medpac (see **Medpacs**). When a creature’s health is reduced to 0, they are dead, and when a vehicle’s health is reduced to 0, it is destroyed. However, when a Spartan’s health is reduced to 0, they instead fall unconscious (see **Death**). 

Shields  
Many creatures and vehicles possess Shields in addition to their base health. Shields are a semi-tangible energy field that protects a creature from harm. When a creature with shields takes damage from an attack, they take the damage directly to their shields instead of their health, only taking damage to their health if they have 0 shields remaining with the exception of certain damage types (such as Hardlight). The Primary advantage of shields is that they can regenerate at a much faster rate than a creature’s health. When a creature with shields goes one full round of combat without taking any new damage to their shields, they regain up to half of their maximum shields (rounded down) at the start of their turn, even if they have no shields remaining. You only gain the benefits of shields while wearing armor.

Medpacs  
All Spartans can carry up to 3 medpacs at any given time and can be used to heal health. The amount healed is equal to half the amount of a Medicinal interaction (rounded down), including all bonuses.

Death  
Creatures are killed when they are reduced to 0 health. A Spartan, on the other hand, is merely exposed to the Unconscious effect at 0 health. When a Spartan reaches 0 health, they are exposed to the Unconscious effect until they die, regain health in any way, or any ally uses the Revive Operation. While the Spartan is unconscious, they can continue to lose health, potentially bringing them to a negative health value. When a Spartan’s health reaches a negative amount equal to their maximum base health, they die permanently. In addition, on each of their turns after being exposed to the Unconscious effect, the damage dice for the attack that brought the Spartan to 0 health are rerolled, and they continue to take damage from the attack until the Unconscious effect ends or they die. An ally may use a Primary Operation to revive an unconscious Spartan, giving them 10 health and exposing them to the Wounded effect.

Dodging   
A Dodge Roll is a roll made to avoid an attack. When a creature is targeted by an attack, they must make a dodge roll by rolling a d100 against the Dodge DC of the weapon the attack was made with. A successful dodge roll means they take no damage, while a failed dodge roll means they suffer the damage dealt by the attack. 

1s and 100s on Dodges  
When a creature rolls a 1 or 100 on a dodge, special circumstances take place. When a creature rolls a 1 on a dodge, they are exposed to the Fallen effect and must spend a Primary Operation to get back up as well as half of their movement speed (rounded down), as stated by the Fallen effect. In the event that a 100 is rolled, they are exposed to the Indomitable effect until the end of their next turn. All creatures are exposed to these effects if they roll a 1 or 100\. These effects do not apply to vehicles.

Chance Attack  
A Chance Attack is a special kind of attack. If a creature moves within 15 feet of a hostile creature then that hostile creature may make a single attack against that creature as a Reactive Operation, provided they are not surprised by that creature and are within range of their current weapon. 

Calling Shots  
When making an attack with any weapon that does not deal explosive damage, a creature may call their shot prior to making the attack. When doing so, they can use any of their attacks with that weapon to fire at specific parts of the target with a specific penalty. Creatures of different sizes may be more difficult to hit in certain spots, and thus get extra bonuses to their dodge rolls against called shots. Small creatures add \+5 to dodges against called shots, and large creatures subtract \-5. The penalties for different types of called shots as well as the effects the target suffers on a hit are listed below. 

**Legs:**   
Penalty: \-15 Dodge DC  
Effects: On a hit, deal the weapon’s damage and decrease the creature’s speed by \-10 feet, which lasts until the target regains health in any way.

**Arms:**   
Penalty: \-25 Dodge DC  
Effects: On a hit, deal the weapon’s damage and decrease the Dodge DC of the creature’s attacks made with the use of their arms or anything they are holding in their arms by 10\. Additionally, on a hit, roll a d6. On a 1, the creature drops any object they are holding, and must expend half their movement in addition to their Tertiary Operation to pick it up. These effects last until the target regains health in any way.

**Head:**  
Penalty: \-35 Dodge DC  
Effects: On a hit, add an extra amount of damage die equal to the base weapon damage.

Precision Weapons  
Certain weapons are designated as Precision weapons. Weapons with this designation are more accurate and more effective at hitting called shots. The bonuses they get to doing so are detailed in the weapon’s statistics.

Damage Types  
**Kinetic:** The most basic of damage types. Kinetic damage is dealt by physical blows, such as bullets, blades, fists, and falling.   
**Acid:** Damage taken from exposure to corrosive chemicals or other agents that would cause burning or abrasion, such as being digested by an enormous beast. Creatures who take acid damage with no shields suffer an additional \+2 damage die.   
**Explosive:** Explosive damage is dealt by rockets, grenades and other explosive materials. Explosive damage is unique in that vehicles suffer full damage from explosive attacks (for more information, see Vehicles).   
**Hardlight:** Hardlight is a special kind of damage inflicted by Hard-Light weapons (weapons that fire a projectile composed of solid light, such as the Light Rifle). When Hardlight damage is dealt to a shielded target, one damage die can be inflicted directly to the target’s base health, ignoring shields.   
**Plasma:** Plasma is a special sort of damage dealt primarily by Covenant weaponry. Plasma weapons are extra effective against shields, dealing an extra \+1 damage die to shields but \-1 damage dice to base health. If an attack dealing plasma damage were to reduce a target’s shields to 0, only half of the remaining damage (rounded down) would be dealt to the target’s health.  
**Shock:** Shock damage generally includes damage from electrical sources, such as stun grenades. When exposed to shock damage, in addition to the damage dealt, the target must succeed on a Fortitude interaction, the DC of which is dependent on the source of the damage, or lose their Secondary and Tertiary Operations. On a successful check, the target loses no Operations.  
**Thermal:** Thermal damage refers to damage suffered as a result of extremely high temperatures, such as from fire and flames. When a creature takes thermal damage, they take the same amount of damage at the end of each of their successive turns unless they expend their Primary, Secondary, and Tertiary Operations to extinguish themselves, ending the damage. If a creature is affected by multiple sources of Thermal damage, they take the damage from each of the sources at the end of each turn, but end all damage when they decide to extinguish themselves.

Attacking Through Allies and Other Creatures  
If an attack passes through a space already occupied by a creature, that creature must make a dodge roll against the attack with an additional \+30 Dodge Bonus to their roll (provided they are aware of the attack) or be hit by the attack instead of the target. If the creature is not aware of the attack, they make the dodge at the normal Dodge DC.

**Special Circumstances in Combat: Cover, Surprise, Difficult Terrain, Et Cetera**

Surprise  
When a creature makes an attack against a target that is unaware of its presence, the target is exposed to the Surprised effect until the start of its next turn, but is made aware of its attacker. Additionally, if it is surprised by all enemy creatures involved in combat, they lose \-20 to their initiative rolls for that instance of combat. 

Difficult Terrain  
Some areas may be deemed as difficult terrain by the GM. In these areas, all creatures’ speed is halved (rounded down). Some examples of potentially difficult terrain are waist deep water, some mountainous areas, or other places that could make a creature travel slower. If they are attempting to move through the space of a creature, that is also classified as difficult terrain. Creatures cannot move through the space of any hostile creatures unless that creature has been exposed to the Fallen effect, in which case moving through that creature’s space becomes difficult terrain. Additionally, climbing any objects that the GM determines as climbable counts as difficult terrain unless using *Anti-Gravity Armor* or similar abilities.

Picking up Objects  
For a creature to pick up any dropped object, such as a weapon that has been knocked out of their hand or a small item that has been discarded, they must take the Interact Operation, which requires them to spend their Tertiary Operation to pick the item up.

Dual Wielding  
Certain weapons can be dual wielded. If a creature has a weapon in each hand, they can choose to make one additional attack as a Secondary Operation using the weapon in their second hand while still making the normal amount of attacks with the weapon in their first hand. A weapon can only be dual wielded if it has the “Dual Wielding” trait listed in its statistics.

Nonlethal Damage  
To administer non-lethal damage, you must make a called shot against either the arms or legs when using a weapon. When making a melee attack, you can choose to make the damage nonlethal without having to make any called shots. When a creature is reduced to 0 health with nonlethal damage they are exposed to the Unconscious effect instead of being killed.

Cover  
The Game Master might decide that some barriers, such as a wall, are penetrable by bullets or certain weapons. All barriers will fall under 1 of 7 categories of cover. Each level of cover has a threshold of health for each 10 foot segment. When a segment of cover’s health is entirely depleted, it is destroyed, and becomes difficult terrain occupying the same space as where the cover previously stood, ending all benefits to creatures standing behind the segment of cover. 

It is possible for attacks to penetrate cover to hit the creatures behind. A creature attempting to shoot through cover must reduce the damage of their attack by a certain number of dice depending on the level of cover, and the target creature receives a bonus to dodge rolls made against the attacks. In this case, the source of cover takes an amount of damage equal to half of the damage rolled (rounded down) after the damage die reduction. If the damage die reduction exceeds the amount of damage die the weapon deals on a standard attack, then the weapon cannot penetrate the cover or target creatures behind it. Alternatively, a creature may choose to attack the segment of cover directly, dealing full damage to the cover without any dodge roll required. 

**Flimsy (1-50 Health):**  
	*Target Dodge:* \+5  
*Damage Die Reduction:* N/A  
	*Examples:* Light foliage, cloth   
**Weak (51-100 Health):**   
*Target Dodge:* \+10  
*Damage Die Reduction:* 1  
	*Examples:* Glass, brittle wood  
**Average (101-150 Health):**   
*Target Dodge:* \+15  
*Damage Die Reduction:* 2  
*Examples:* Tile, plaster  
**Sturdy (151-225 Health):**   
*Target Dodge:* \+20  
*Damage Die Reduction:* 3  
*Examples:* Brick, cement  
**Solid (226-300 Health):**   
*Target Dodge:* \+25  
*Damage Die Reduction:* 4  
	*Examples:* Stone, concrete  
**Strong (301-450 Health):**  
*Target Dodge:* \+30  
*Damage Die Reduction:* 5  
 	*Examples:* Metal, ore  
**Unassailable (451+ Health):**   
*Target Dodge:* Cannot be targeted with attacks  
*Damage Die Reduction:* N/A  
	*Examples:* Reinforced metal

Downtime  
Downtime is any period of time no shorter than 6 hours spent by the Fireteam when they are not in immediate danger (such as combat) and not performing strenuous physical activity, such as intense labor. After a period of downtime, all creatures regain all health and shields previously lost, as well as recharging any abilities with limited usage, such as Active Camo or Armor Lock

Zero Gravity  
Some scenarios will have creatures working and fighting in 0 gravity. While in 0 gravity, all creatures’ speeds are halved (rounded down). However they can move vertically as well as horizontally. Fly speeds are unaffected by this penalty. In addition, while in 0 gravity you cannot be exposed to the Fallen effect.

Underwater  
When in water too deep for a creature to stand in, they are exposed to the following effects:

- Movement speed is halved  
- \-20 to all dodges  
- The range of your weapon is halved  
- Your melee damage is halved  
- Cannot be exposed to the Fallen effect

A Spartan’s suit retains enough oxygen to survive underwater unassisted for up to 5 minutes.

In Darkness  
Some instances in the game may have creatures in dark effects. There are three degrees of darkness with different penalties, there are as follows:

Dim Light:   
\-5 to weapon and melee Dodge DC and Detection, Tracking, and Tactics interactions  
\+5 to all Stealth interactions  
Darkness:   
	\-10 to weapon and melee Dodge DC and Detection, Tracking, and Tactics interactions  
\+10 to all Stealth interactions  
If you use more than half of your movement on your turn you must make a DC 30 dodge or be  
or be exposed to the Fallen effect.  
Void:   
\-15 to weapon/melee Dodge DC and Detection, Tracking, and Tactics interactions  
           \+15 to all Stealth interactions  
	If you use more than half of your movement in one turn you must make a DC 40 dodge  
or be exposed to the Fallen effect.

Fall Damage  
In some instances, creatures may have the misfortune to fall great distances. The damage taken from falling is equal to 4 (1d6) for every 10 feet fallen, with a cap at 40d6 at a height of 400 feet. If the GM determines a fall to be from an unreasonably high height, such as falling from orbit, they are within their authority to simply declare the falling creature dead on impact with no damage dealt. 

Exhaustion  
At the GM’s discretion, creatures may become exposed to exhaustion, representing extreme, sustained physical exertion without rest. When exposed to exhaustion, a creature suffers a \-5 penalty to their movement speed, dodge rolls, and any interactions they make. Exhaustion is cumulative, meaning that a creature already suffering from exhaustion who is exposed to exhaustion again suffers an additional \-5 penalty to the above attributes. If a creature is exposed to enough exhaustion to reduce their speed to 0, they are exposed to the Unconscious effect, and if they suffer any further exhaustion before resting during downtime, they die. All exhaustion levels suffered by a creature are removed after resting during downtime. 

## Interactions

Certain classes can interact with certain objects that are within their fields. The GM will decide what field a certain interaction is in. These fields are as follows:

**Agility**   
Agility concerns reflexes, manual dexterity, and acrobatic acumen. Agility interactions could be made for a number of circumstances, such as attempting to jump a great height or distance, to extricate oneself from restraints, pick a mechanical lock, or similar tasks. 

**Crafting**  
Crafting interactions can be used to make and repair technology or other mundane devices. Crafting can encompass tasks as complex as repairing an engine or as simple as shaping a stone axe. While not as useful in combat as other interactions, a creative Spartan can make great use of this skill while not in the throes of battle. 

**Charisma**  
Charisma interactions are made to convince, haggle, deceive, negotiate, or otherwise alter the attitudes of another creature.

**Demolition**  
Demolition interactions involve the understanding, identification, maintenance, and use of explosive devices such as mines, grenades, artillery shells, and more. Demolition interactions may be required to properly use, set, or detonate certain explosive devices. 

**Detection**   
Detection interactions pertain to spatial awareness. Detection interactions are necessary when attempting to locate a creature or object, or notice visual, olfactory, or auditory stimuli. Detection interactions may also be necessary when attempting to discern a creature or object that is hidden or obscured. 

**Firepower**   
Firepower interactions encompass a mechanical and practical understanding of firearms and related weaponry such as energy weapons, kinetic weapons, large-scale weapons such as MAC-Cannons and artillery batteries. Firepower interactions could be used to identify, maintain, and modify such weaponry. 

**Fortitude**  
Stamina, hardiness, and endurance are all represented by Fortitude. Fortitude interactions may be called for to resist debilitating effects such as poisons, harsh weather, extreme temperatures, or physically demanding tasks. 

**Handling**  
When attempting to manipulate or control vehicles, you may be required to make a Handling interaction. This could be for calming a riding horse or trying to jump a large gap with a warthog.

**History**   
When attempting to recall a fact from earlier times, or any other piece of knowledge that took place in the past, you may need to roll a history check. This can encompass such things as names, dates and basic facts, but also more specific things such as recent military Operations or newsworthy events.

**Lifting**  
Many activities that involve general strength will require a lifting roll. This can include lifting, moving and pulling heavy objects, but it can also be used for combat maneuvers like grappling.

**Medicinal**   
Recalling and utilizing medical knowledge falls under this interaction. Both an understanding of medicine, such as anatomy, biochemistry, psychology, etc, and medical skills such as first aid, administering medpacs, creating medicinal items, etc. would fall in this field. 

**Stealth**   
When attempting to go unnoticed, a Stealth interaction will be necessary. Stealth interactions involve obscuring oneself, whether moving, stationary, or attempting to keep actions hidden from observers. 

**Tactics**  
Tactics interactions involve observing and analyzing the battlefield, as well as using this analysis to create strategies to more effectively work with other members of your fireteam. Tactic interactions may involve identifying adequate cover, anticipating an enemy’s next move, coordinating with teammates, or navigating battlefield hazards.

**Tech**   
Any interactions that involve attempting to use, decipher, or identify a technological device require a Tech interaction. 

**Tracking**   
Tracking encompasses all skills used to follow a creature that you have lost sight of or have only evidence of such as footprints, blood trails, or particularly strong scents. The difficulty of these checks may vary over different types of terrain such as mud, snow, or stone.

Interactions are based on the tier of difficulty of the interaction. These tiers are:

Easy- DC 40  
Mediocre- DC 65  
Medium- DC 80  
Hard- DC 105  
Extremely Challenging- DC 130  
Close to impossible- DC 150

A roll of 100 on any of these is an immediate success, while a 1 is an immediate fail. At the GM’s discretion, rolling a 100 may be considered a “critical success” and provide additional benefits, or rolling a 1 may be considered a “critical failure” and invoke additional penalties. 

Improving Interactions  
At certain levels, you may have the opportunity to gain “Interaction Points.” The Spartan can distribute these Interaction Points across their Interactions, with each point giving a permanent \+1 bonus to that Interaction. Additionally, as you rank up, the bonus to Interactions that you have superiority or expertise in will increase.

Interaction Contests  
Certain game instances may involve an interaction contest between two creatures. When this happens, both creatures must perform a given interaction and compare their result, adding any applicable modifiers. The creature with the higher total wins the contest, with ties being won by the targeted creature. 

## Superiorities and Expertises

Spartans, as a result of their training, will have fields that they specialize in, granting them additional bonuses when making certain interactions. These bonuses are classified as either a Superiority (S), representing a minor bonus accrued through study and practice in a field, or Expertise (E), representing a large bonus gained from a great deal of knowledge and experience in a given field. The individual bonuses associated with Superiority and Expertise increase with the Spartan’s rank, as shown on the table below. 

Second Lieutenant: S= \+5, E= \+10  
First Lieutenant: S= \+5, E= \+10  
Captain: S= \+5, E= \+10  
Major: S= \+10, E= \+20  
Lieutenant-Colonel: S= \+10, E= \+20  
Colonel-Major: S= \+15, E= \+30  
Field Marshal: S= \+15, E= \+30  
Lieutenant-General: S= \+20, S= \+40  
General-Major: S= \+20, E= \+40  
Commander: S= \+25, E= \+50  
Fleet-Commander: S= \+25, E= \+50  
Hyper-Lethal Vector:S= \+30, E= \+60

# Combat Maneuvers

In combat, creatures are capable of making quick maneuvers in the heat of battle. During combat situations, you may forgo your Primary, Secondary or Tertiary Operations to perform one of these maneuvers to gain the upper hand in a fight. The options are as follows:

**Identify:**  
Cost: Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Identify maneuver, make a DC 50 History interaction targeting 1 creature within 60 feet. On a success, you may learn 1 piece of information that you ask of the GM within reason.

**Move:**  
Cost: Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Move maneuver, you target 1 friendly and willing creature within 30 feet and instruct them to move up to 5 feet in any direction, not counting against their movement.

**Survey:**  
Cost: Tertiary Operation  
Effect: You survey the battlefield to try to find enemies, search for weak points in structures, and other such effects. Make a Detection interaction determined by the GM. While this maneuver is primarily Detection, it can be replaced with other interactions in certain cases, such as identifying what weapon an enemy is carrying with Firepower or what a piece of technology is with Tech.

**Switch:**  
Cost: Tertiary Operation, 5 feet of Movement  
Effect: When taking the Switch maneuver, you switch places with 1 creature of medium size or smaller within 5 feet. If the creature is not willing, make a Lifting or Agility (player’s choice) contest. On a success, your places are swapped.

**Draw Fire:**  
Cost: Secondary Operation   
Effect: When taking the Draw Fire maneuver, make a Charisma contest against one creature within 30 feet. On a success, the creature turns its attention to you and attacks you on their turn provided you are within range and the creature can see you.

**Hull Pierce:**  
Cost: Secondary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Hull Pierce maneuver, make a DC 50 Handling interaction against 1 vehicle within 60 feet. On a success your next attack against that vehicle does full damage. If your attack already deals full damage it instead deals \+2 additional damage die.  
   
**Prepare:**  
Cost: Secondary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Prepare maneuver, you gain an additional Reactionary Operation until the start of your next turn.

**Push:**   
Cost: Secondary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Push maneuver, you move a creature within 5 feet by an amount depending on their size. Small creatures can be moved up to 15 feet, Medium creatures up to 10 feet and Large creatures up to 5 feet. Massive creatures cannot be targeted by this maneuver. If the creature is not willing, make a Lifting contest. On a success, the creature is pushed away.

**Brace:**  
Cost: Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Brace maneuver, the next attack made against you deals half damage (rounded down).

**Disarm:**  
Cost: Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Disarm maneuver, you make a Lifting contest with a creature within 5 feet. On a success, the weapon is knocked out of their hands and lands within 5 feet of them.

**Feint:**  
Cost: Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Feint maneuver, make a Stealth contest against a creature within 30 feet. On a success, the creature is exposed to the Surprised effect for your next attack. 

**Intimidate:**  
Cost: Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation   
Effect: When taking the Intimidate maneuver, make a Charisma contest against a creature within 30 feet. On a success the target is exposed to the Frightened effect until the start of your next turn. On a failure, the creature is immune to your Intimidate maneuver for 24 hours.

**Knockdown:**   
Cost: Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Knockdown maneuver, make a Lifting or Agility contest (Player’s Choice) with 1 creature within 5 feet. On a failure, the creature is exposed to the Fallen effect.

**Recover:**  
Cost: Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Recover maneuver, make a Tech interaction. You recover an amount of shields equal to 10 \+ the result of the interaction roll divided by 10 (rounded down). 

**Scramble:**   
Cost: Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Scramble maneuver, you don’t trigger chance attacks until the start of your next turn.

**Shelter:**  
Cost: Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Shelter maneuver, make a DC 50 Tactics interaction. On a success, you may treat any cover you are behind as 1 level higher for yourself only. Additionally this maneuver does not change the health of the cover. This effect is lost at the start of your next turn or when you move out of the cover you are sheltered behind.

**Dash:**  
Cost: Primary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Dash maneuver, double your movement speed for that turn.

**Hide:**  
Cost: Primary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Hide maneuver, if you are within 5 feet of cover or anything you could reasonably hide behind or in, make a Stealth interaction. Any creatures that are aware of you must, on the beginning of their next turn, make a Detection interaction that equals or exceeds the result of your Stealth interaction. On a failure, you are successfully hidden from that creature and cannot be targeted by any attacks from them while in cover. This maneuver   
lasts until you leave cover or a creature succeeds their Detection interaction. This Detection Interaction can

**Ready Up:**  
Cost: Primary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Ready Up maneuver, you are exposed to the Alert effect until the end of your next turn.

**Throw:**   
Cost: Primary Operation  
Effect: When making the Throw maneuver, you can throw an object weighing up to 25 pounds up to 30 feet with Dodge DC 50. On a hit, the object does damage equal to its poundage divided by 5 in d6.

**Ground Pound:**  
Cost: Primary Operation, 10 feet of Height, 20 feet of Movement  
If a creature jumps off of a platform at least 10 feet above the ground, they may use their Primary Operation to slam into an enemy within 15 feet of the platform, dealing 5d12 kinetic damage to the target and exposing them to the Fallen effect if they fail a Dodge DC 60\. Every creature within 5 feet must also make a DC 60 dodge or take half damage (rounded down) and be exposed to the Fallen effect if the dodge is failed. On a successful dodge, the creature making the Ground Pound maneuver will take an amount of fall damage dependent on how far they fell. Additionally, for every additional 5 feet higher the ground pound is made from, the creature may add an additional \+7 (1d12) kinetic damage. In addition to a Primary Operation, you must also expend 20 feet of your movement to make this attack.

**Gambit:**  
Cost: Primary Operation, Secondary Operation  
Effect: When making the Gambit maneuver, make a DC 65 Firepower interaction. On a success, if your weapon can make 2 or more attacks you may make 1 additional attack on your turn. On a failure, your gun jams and you must use a Secondary Operation to fix your weapon and continue using it.

**Quick Footed:**   
Cost: Primary Operation, Secondary Operation  
Effect: When making the Quick Footed maneuver, make a DC 50 Tracking interaction. On a success you and all allies within 30 feet gain \+15 movement speed and can ignore difficult terrain.

**Prime:**  
Cost: Primary Operation, Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation (Optional), Grenade  
Effect: When making the Prime maneuver, make DC 50 Demolition interaction. On a success you can throw a grenade and increase its radius by 5 feet. Additionally, you can choose 1 other Primary target of the grenade that is within 5 feet of the original Primary target. However, on a failure the grenade will explode in your hand unless you use a Tertiary Operation in addition to the Primary and Secondary Operations.

**Fortify:**   
Cost: Primary Operation, Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Fortify maneuver, roll a Fortitude interaction and divide the result by 5\. Until the start of your next turn you may subtract damage taken from each attack equal to this amount.

**Grapple:**  
Cost: Primary Operation, Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When taking the Grapple maneuver, you target one creature within 5 feet and have a Lifting contest with them. On a failure the creature is exposed to the Grappled effect.

**Warcry:**  
Cost: Primary Operation, Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation  
Effect: When making the Warcry maneuver, all friendly creatures within 30 feet gain \+5 to their Dodge DCs, \+5 Dodge bonus, and \+5 speed until the end of your next turn.

**All In:**  
Cost: Primary Operation, Secondary Operation, Tertiary Operation, All Movement  
Effect: When taking the All In maneuver, you expend all your movement speed towards 1 target and make all of your attacks at that 1 target. The Dodge DC of your attacks are increased by \+15, and all attacks that hit gain an extra damage die. If you reduce that creature’s health to 0, you may target another creature within range with all remaining attacks while still benefiting from these buffs.

# Rank

**Rank**  
As you complete missions, your rank will go up. As you climb the ranks, you will gain access to new abilities and techniques that will make your Spartan more efficient in and out of combat. These experiences will fundamentally change your Spartan, making them faster, stronger, and smarter. Every time you rank up you are given a selection of new abilities to choose from and may choose one ability from the list. (except for the starting ability which is given upon choosing the class). These ranks and their unlocks are as follows:

**2nd Lieutenant:** Starting ability, Stat increase  
**1st Lieutenant:** General equipment/abilities  
**Captain:** Special equipment/abilities  
**Major:** Superiority/expertise increase, Stat increase  
**Lieutenant-Colonel:** General equipment/abilities  
**Colonel-Major:** Special equipment/abilities  
**Field Marshal:** Stat increase  
**Lieutenant-General:** Superiority/expertise increase, General equipment/abilities  
**General-Major:** Special equipment/abilities  
**Commander:** Stat increase  
**Fleet-Commander:** General equipment/abilities  
**Hyper-Lethal Vector:** Superiority/expertise increase, Special equipment/abilities

Ability Exchange  
Every time you rank up you are given the choice of switching one of your abilities. Each time your rank increases, you may select one ability and exchange it for another ability of the same rank within your class.

Gun and Grenade  Slots  
Each Spartan has a certain amount of gun slots. Different weapons take up a different amount of slots as determined by their size. The same is true for grenades. Each Spartan has a limited amount of grenade slots and each individual grenade takes up a single grenade slot. If a Spartan attempts to carry more guns or grenades than they have slots for, their speed is halved and they suffer \-20 to all dodges. The amount of gun slots each size of weapon requires is listed below:

**Small:** ½   
**Medium:** 1  
**Large:** 2  
**Massive:** 3

# Effects

**Alert:** Any creature exposed to the Alert effect has a \+25 to dodges and Detection interactions.  
**Blinded:** Any creature exposed to the Blinded effect is unable to see and as a result suffers a \-30 penalty to all dodge rolls as well as a \-15 penalty to the Dodge DCs of any attacks they make while blinded. Additionally, if the creature moves more than 10 feet in a single turn while blinded, it must succeed on a DC 45 Agility interaction or become exposed to the Fallen effect.   
**Deafened:** Any creature exposed to this cannot hear and automatically fails any actions that rely on hearing.   
**Fallen:** Any creature exposed to this effect will be knocked down, and have a \-20 to all dodges. Any creature exposed to the Fallen effect must expend half of their movement (rounded down) on their turn to end this effect. If you choose to move without ending this effect, treat all movement as difficult terrain.  
**Frightened:** Any creature exposed to the Frightened effect must roll a d4 at the beginning of their turn. Depending on the roll of the dice, the affected creature is exposed to a random outcome.

1. The Frightened creature must spend all of its Movement speed to move away from the creature or object it is frightened by.  
2. The Frightened creature’s Movement speed is reduced to 0\.  
3. The Frightened creature must attack the creature that frightened it. Any attacks made by the Frightened creature have a \-15 penalty to Dodge DCs.  
4. The creature loses all Operations.

**Grappled:** Any creature exposed to the Grappled effect has their speed set to 0, and exposed to the Incapacitated effect.  
**Incapacitated:** Any creature exposed to the Incapacitated effect has a \-35 to dodges, and any attacks made by an Incapacitated creature have their Dodge DC reduced by \-15. Incapacitated creatures must spend a Primary Operation to move any distance.  
**Indomitable:** Any creature exposed to this effect gains the following benefits.   
\-Add \+15 to dodge  
\-Add \+10 feet of movement speed  
\-Extra Secondary and Tertiary Operation  
\-Add \+2 damage to all attacks  
**Invisible:** Any creature exposed to the Invisible effect gains an additional \+20 bonus to all dodges and Stealth interactions. This bonus to dodge and Stealth interactions is reduced by \-5 every time the creature takes damage while exposed to the Invisible effect. When the bonus to dodge and Stealth interactions is reduced to 0, the effect immediately ends.   
**Poisoned:** Make a Fortitude interaction with a DC determined by the source of the effect. If the interaction fails, the creature is exposed to the Poisoned effect. While this effect lasts, the creature suffers a \-5 penalty to dodge rolls. In addition, when exposed to the Poisoned effect, the creature may only make half as many attacks (rounded down) with your weapons per turn. If this would cause a weapon to have less than one attack per turn, then that weapon requires forfeiture of your next Primary Operation to attack with, effectively making that weapon only able to be used once every other round until the effect ends. At the start of each of your turns, you may repeat the Fortitude interaction, ending the effect on a success.   
**Stunned:** Any creature exposed to the Stunned effect is rendered completely immobile, losing all of its movement speed, and suffers a \-40 to all dodges. The creature also cannot take any Operations.  
**Surprised:** A surprised creature has a \-25 to dodges made against creatures it is unaware of.  
**Unconscious:** Any creature exposed to the Unconscious effect is unable to take any Operations, and is exposed to the Incapacitated effect. An ally using a Primary Operation to revive the affected creature ending both the Unconscious and Incapacitated effects.  
**Wounded:** Any creature exposed to the Wounded effect has their movement speed halved (rounded down) and has \-10 to all dodges. This effect lasts until the health of the creature is healed in any way. If a creature exposed to the Wounded effect goes Unconscious they gain a tier of Exhaustion.

# Battlefield Externalities

Every battlefield has its own unpredictability. At initiative 0, a randomly determined effect will happen on the battlefield. The effect is determined by rolling a d20 and lasts until initiative 0 happens again. These effects on the table are incredibly general and it is up to the GM to properly flavor them to fit the situation. For example, they could explain everyone’s Dodge DC increasing due to a heavy arctic wind passing through. Note: it is not necessary to roll on this table every turn. The GM can pick and choose which effects happen. The potential effects are:

| 1 | All combatants have the Dodge DC increased by 10\. |
| :---- | :---- |
| 2 | Combatants within a 20 foot radius have to succeed on a Dodge DC 50 or take 11 (3d6) damage. |
| 3 | When combatants move through a specific area within a 20 foot radius, their movement speed is increased by 5 feet. |
| 4 | One random damage type deals an extra die of damage for the duration of the fight. |
| 5 | One random creature heals 11 (3d6) health. |
| 6 | One random creature takes 21 (6d6) damage. |
| 7 | One random vehicle ceases to function and cannot be operated. |
| 8 | All terrain in a 20 foot radius becomes difficult terrain. |
| 9 | All creatures within a 20 foot radius have to succeed on a Dodge DC 50 or be exposed to the deafened effect.  |
| 10 | All creatures within a 20 foot radius have to succeed on a Dodge DC 50 or be exposed to the blinded effect.  |
| 11 | All creatures within a 20 foot radius have to succeed on a Dodge DC 50 or be exposed to the fallen effect.  |
| 12 | All creatures within a 20 foot radius have to succeed on a Dodge DC 50 or be exposed to the frightened effect.  |
| 13 | Up to three random creatures have to succeed on a Dodge DC 50 or be exposed to the grappled effect. |
| 14 | All creatures must succeed on a Dodge DC 50 or have their current shield health be depleted by 50%. |
| 15 | All creatures get an extra Tertiary Operation. |
| 16 | All creatures get an extra Secondary Operation. |
| 17 | All terrain in a 20 foot radius deals 14 (3d8) damage to any creature in it or that walks through it |
| 18 | One random weapon ceases to function and cannot be operated. |
| 19 | One random turret ceases to function and cannot be operated. |
| 20 | All creatures get an extra Primary Operation. |

# Fireteam Members

This is a list of all the playable character classes in Break of Dawn. This includes all of their abilities, health, starting weapons, and other attributes.

![[Assassin]]

The grass rustles as a Spartan armed only with a knife soundlessly sneaks up on his prey; an elite shipmaster. As he comes up behind him, the elite only has time for a single muffled scream before his throat is slit by the Assassin’s knife. With his objective accomplished, he slinks back into the grass, waiting for his next victim. He is an assassin, a precision oriented class that stalks its prey and eliminates them with an array of specialized melee weaponry in addition to standard firearms.

**Statistics:**  
Health: 30  
Shields: 35  
Health per rank up: 4 (1d6)  
Speed: 45 feet  
Size: Medium  
Recommended Starting Weaponry: A Shotgun and a Magnum Pistol  
Superiorities: Tracking, Charisma  
Expertises: Stealth, Agility  
Gun Carrying Capacity: You have 3 gun slots  
Grenade Capacity: You have 5 grenade slots

**Starting Abilities:** *Assassinate*. When you make a melee attack against a creature exposed to the Surprised effect, you may add an additional \+22 (4d10) kinetic damage.  
                              *Combat Knife.* You have a knife you may use instead of the normal melee ability. The knife can be thrown up to 20 feet with a dodge of 50 dealing the same amount of kinetic damage as a melee attack but does not count as a melee attack. 

2nd Lieutenant:  
**Hearty:** Add \+4 to your base health.  
**Improved Shields:** Add \+3 to your base shields.  
**Extended Grenade Belt**: Add \+1 grenade slot.  
**Extended Hip Holster:** Add \+1 gun slot.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+5 Interaction Points.

1st Lieutenant:  
**Fast:** Gain an extra \+5 movement speed.  
**Suppressor:** Ranged weapon attacks you make cannot be heard by creatures further than 10 feet away from you.   
**Agile:** Add \+5 to all dodges.

Captain:  
**Improved Combat Knife:** You have improved your skills with knives. The Dodge DC of your knife increases to 65 when held or thrown. Additionally, the *Assassinate* ability applies to thrown knives.  
**Hide in the Shadows:** When in complete darkness, you may roll a Stealth interaction. No matter the result, you are exposed to the Invisible effect. However, a creature that makes a Detection interaction that has a higher total than your stealth roll is able to see you. This ability does not protect you from thermal imaging.    
**Nimble:** You do not trigger chance attacks when moving. Additionally, you gain a \+10 to all dodges.

Major:  
**Hearty:** Add \+7 to your base health.  
**Improved Shields:** Add \+5 to your base shields.  
**Extended Grenade Belt:** Add \+1 grenade slot.  
**Extended Hip Holster:** Add \+1 gun slot.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+10 Interaction Points.

Lieutenant Colonel:  
**Camouflage:** When making a Stealth interaction to hide, you may add an additional \+15 to the roll. Additionally, all creatures have a \-10 to Detection interactions while attempting to locate you.  
**Cloaking Devices:** 3 times per downtime, you can place a cloaking device on an object that could fit inside a 3 ft x 3 ft x 3 ft cube. The object will then be invisible to the naked eye, visible only with thermal imaging or similar technology. The object will remain invisible for up to one hour or until the cloaking devices are deactivated. It can be activated or deactivated remotely if you are within 2 miles of the object, however, the device must be attached manually.   
**Thermal Imaging Goggles:** Twice per downtime, for a minute each, you can activate thermal imaging goggles in your helmet that allow you to see and locate the thermal imaging of any creature within 60 feet, penetrating only through light underbrush and similar obstructions. These goggles allow you to ignore any penalties imposed by fighting in darkness. You can also read the current health and strength of the shields on up to 5 creatures.

Colonel Major:  
**Improved Melee**: The Dodge DC of your melee attacks increases by 15\.  
**Twist of Fate:** Twice per downtime when you fail a dodge you can choose to succeed instead.  
**Weapons Experts:** You may select up to two weapons of small size which you have grown akin to using. You may now use the *Assassinate* ability with their attacks.

Field Marshal:  
**Hearty:** Add \+15 to base health.  
**Improved Shields:** Add \+12 to base shields.  
**Extended Grenade Belt:** Add \+2 grenade slots.  
**Extended Hip Holster:** Add \+2 gun slots.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+15 Interaction Points.

Lieutenant General:  
**Tripwire:** You have a tripwire that you can place as a Primary Operation, creating a line up to 20 feet long that requires a DC 85 detection check for someone who isn’t aware of its presence to find. Anyone who walks through  it must make a DC 80 dodge or be exposed to the fallen effect.  
**False Identity:** You have become skilled at the art of imitating others’ appearances. You can use an hour of downtime to transform your appearance into that of another creature of the same size category as you. At a glance, your appearance is indiscernible from that of which you are imitating, however upon closer inspection, some faults can be detected. When your disguise is inspected closely, you must make a Charisma check against the inspecting creature’s Detection check. On a success, they fall for your disguise, however, on a fail, the inspecting creature can see through the disguise.  
**Strike From the Shadows:**  When attacking a creature exposed to the Surprised effect, your first attack grants an extra amount of damage die equal to the base weapon damage.

General Major:  
**Assassination Expert**: When using your *Assassinate* ability, add an additional \+22 (4d10) kinetic damage to the base damage, additionally the Dodge DC for punch/stab attacks made against surprised enemies increases by \+10.  
**Active Camo:** Twice per downtime, as a Tertiary Operation you may activate an invisibility module within your suit. When activated, you and any equipment you were carrying at the time of its activation are exposed to the Invisible effect. This lasts for up to a minute or until you end it as a Secondary Operation or make a weapon attack.   
**Martial Arts Expert:** When you make a stab/punch attack, you can make a second attack with a small weapon or another stab/punch attack with \-10 subtracted from the Dodge DC. 

Commander:  
**Heart of a Lion:** Add \+24 to base health, and at the start of each of your turns you regain 5 health as long as you are conscious.  
**Shield of the People:** Add \+19 to your base shields, and once per downtime, you can bring yourself back to full shields as a Tertiary Operation.  
**Loose Cannon:** Add \+3 grenade slots, and the range of all grenades you throw is doubled.  
**Artillery Expert:** Add \+3 gun slots, and you may now take the Change Weapons Operation at will on your turn without having to spend a Tertiary Operation.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+25 Interaction Points.

Fleet Commander:  
**Jack of All Trades:** Select any two abilities of Commander rank or lower.  
**Diversified Tactics:** Select any ability of Commander rank or lower from any class’s list.  
**Off the Grid:** You cannot be detected by any technology that reveals your location (radar, thermal imaging goggles, etc).

Hyper-Lethal Vector:  
**Target Acquired:** During combat as a Secondary Operation you may choose an enemy within 30 feet to mark as a target. When attacking a marked target you gain an additional Secondary and Tertiary Operation, provided that all of your attacks and maneuvers are made against that target. Your Dodge DC increases by \+10 for all attacks and maneuvers against that target. If your target exits your melee/stab range, you may use a Reactive Operation to make a melee/stab attack dealing half damage (rounded down). After a target is killed, you can transfer these effects to another creature within 30 feet as a Tertiary Operation.   
**Athlete:** Your body has reached the peak agility of what a Spartan can accomplish and gain the following abilities:  
\-You gain \+15 movement speed  
\-You gain \+15 to all dodges  
\-When you kill an enemy, you can immediately move up to 15 feet in any direction, not    
counting against your movement speed.   
\-The Dodge DC of your punch/stab increases by 10\.

![[commando]]

## Demolitionist

As command gives the order for the enemy base to be blown to smithereens, the Demolitionist happily presses the detonation button, watching the massive explosion in the distance. Seeing a survivor from the explosion, the spartan takes aim for a second, and launches a mortar shell from their shoulder, eliminating the last traces of their attack.

**Statistics:**  
Health: 55  
Shields: 60  
Health per rank up: 6 (1d10)  
Speed: 25 feet  
Size: Medium  
Recommended Starting Weaponry: Grenade Launcher, Magnum Pistol  
Superiorities: Tech, Lifting  
Expertises: Firepower, Demolition  
Gun Carrying Capacity: You have 4 gun slots  
Grenade Capacity: You have 10 grenade slots

**Starting Ability:** *Mortar.* Attached to your shoulder is a small mortar. Once per minute you can fire a shell as a Secondary Operation, with a range of 75 feet, dealing 5d8 Explosive damage, with Dodge DC 60 in a 10 foot radius. Creatures within the explosion radius that succeed on the dodge roll still take half damage (rounded down).

2nd Lieutenant:  
**Hearty:** Add \+9 to your base health  
**Improved Shields:** Add \+5 to your base shields  
**Extended Grenade Belt**: Add \+1 grenade slot  
**Extended Hip Holster:** Add \+1 gun slot  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+5 Interaction Points.

1st Lieutenant:  
**Bulky:** When enemies try to move you against your will, you gain a \+20 to dodges and contests to resist being moved.  
**Fortitude:** Twice per downtime when you take damage, as a Reactive Operation you may roll a d20 and reduce the damage taken by that amount.  
**Vigorous:** You receive a \+20 for any lifting check you make.

Captain:  
**Demolitions Expert:** You can treat all explosive weapons as one size category smaller.  
**Grenadier:** When you use a grenade, its Dodge DC increases by 5, its range increases by 10 feet, and radius increases by 5 feet. Additionally, when you use a Primary Operation to throw a grenade, you may throw a second grenade without expending any Operations.  
**Twice the Pride:** When using a weapon with Detonation or grenade, you may designate a second main target granted that they are within 5 feet of the initial main target.

Major:   
**Hearty:** Add \+17 to your base health.  
**Improved Shields:** Add \+11 to your base shields.  
**Extended Grenade Belt:** Add \+1 grenade slot.  
**Extended Hip Holster:** Add \+1 gun slot.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+10 Interaction Points.

Lieutenant Colonel:  
**Repel:** As a reactionary Operation once every two turns, you may repel a single attack from a medium or smaller weapon that targets you or anything within 5 feet of you. The attacking creature then becomes the target of the attack but that attack’s Dodge DC is decreased by \-15.  
**Portable Energy Shield:** You gain an additional 80 shields, however these shields do not affect your total shield health or the amount of shields regenerated per turn of not taking damage. Instead, these additional shields generate a portable energy shield emanating around you. If the energy shield has between 1 and 30 shields, it grants Weak cover, if it has between 31 and 60 shields it grants Average cover, and if it has between 61 and 80 shields it grants Sturdy cover. If an attack would otherwise hit but is dodged as a result of the bonus provided from the portable energy shield’s cover, the shield takes the full damage of the attack. As a Secondary Operation, you can place this cover down anywhere within 5 feet. When deployed in this way it provides cover in a 15 foot line reaching 10 feet high. Any creatures behind this cover gain its benefits and can make weapon attacks through the shields with no penalty. As a Tertiary Operation, you may also pick the portable energy shield back up.  
**Anti-Gravity Armor:** Once per downtime, expending no Operations, you can activate a series of anti-gravity thrusters for up to ten minutes. These thrusters limit your speed to your base speed \-5 feet, however you can now walk on any surface, such as walls and ceilings. Additionally, difficult terrain does not limit your movement speed and you cannot take fall damage while this is active.

Colonel Major:  
**Enhanced Area Effectiveness:** The Dodge DC for all enemies is increased by \+5 when using explosive weapons and grenades. Additionally, if a non-target fails the dodge by 15 or more, they take full damage instead of half damage.  
**Improved Explosives:** Whenever you hit a target with an explosive weapon, roll a d4. On a 4, roll twice the weapon’s base amount of damage dice.  
**Remote Charges:** Every downtime, you have five remote charges that you may use at will. Each remote charge does 18 (4d8) damage and can be set as Primary Operation. You may detonate these charges at any range within 5 miles of its location. These charges deal double damage to structures of any sort.

Field Marshal:  
**Hearty:** Add \+26 to base health.  
**Improved Shields:** Add \+19 to base shields.  
**Extended Grenade Belt:** Add \+2 grenade slots.  
**Extended Hip Holster:** Add \+2 gun slots.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+15 Interaction Points.

Lieutenant General:  
**Armor Lock:** As a Primary Operation, you may enter into an armor lock where you stay for up to 2 turns or until you end it as a Secondary Operation. During this time you suffer a \-50 to all dodges and have your speed reduced to 0 feet, but you are immune to all damage and negative effects except that which the GM considers unreasonable (such as a nuclear explosion). When you exit armor lock any hostile creature within 5 feet of you must succeed on a Dodge DC 80 or take however much damage you took while armor locked as shock damage (Fortitude DC 60), taking half damage (rounded down) on a successful dodge. This can be done up to twice per downtime.  
**Wrist Rocket:** As a modification to your armor, you may add a small armament of miniature rockets into your wrist plating. The attachment is capable of holding up to 5 rockets at a time, regaining all rockets during downtime. As a Primary Operation, you can fire as many of these rockets at a target as you wish, with each rocket dealing 4d4 explosive damage with a Dodge DC 80\. This attack can be split between multiple targets. For example, if you fire 5 rockets, you can fire 2 at one enemy and 3 on another, or any other combination of your choice.  
**Repelling Pulse:** As a Secondary Operation you can activate a pulse from your armor for up to 3 turns, which can be ended at any point on your turn as no Operation. At the start of your turn any creatures within 20 feet of you must make a dodge or be pushed away. the Dodge DC of this attack and the amount they are pushed away depends on the creature’s size. Small creatures must make a Dodge DC 80 or be pushed 15 feet. Medium creatures must make a Dodge DC 65 or be pushed 10 feet. Large Creatures must make a Dodge DC 50 or be pushed 5 feet. 

General Major:  
**Multi-Mortar:** You gain two more different methods of using your mortar. They are as follows:  
\-Carpet Bombs: You pepper a 25 by 25 foot cube with smaller explosive pellets with a range of 40 feet and Dodge DC of 65\. All creatures within this area take 20 (3d12) explosive damage. Any creatures that succeed take half damage (rounded down).  
\-Homing Missile: You launch a seeking mortar shell that targets an individual target. The shell has a range of 100 feet, has a Dodge DC 85, and deals 33 (6d10) explosive damage. On a successful dodge, the target takes half damage (rounded down)..  
**Shockwaves:** Your explosives now release shockwaves upon ignition. Whenever a creature fails their dodge against an attack made by you with an explosive weapon by 15 or more, they are exposed to the fallen effect. Additionally, you deal double damage to all structures and buildings with explosive weapons.  
**Vehicle Buster:** When attacking a vehicle with explosive weapons, add \+10 to your weapon’s Dodge DC. If the vehicle fails the dodge by 20 or more, you may roll twice the weapon’s base amount of damage dice.

Commander:  
**Heart of a Lion:** Add \+40 to base health, and at the start of each of your turns you regain 5 health as long as you are conscious.  
**Shield of the People:** Add \+33 to your base shields, and once per downtime, you can bring yourself back to full shields as a Tertiary Operation.  
**Loose Cannon:** Add \+3 grenade slots, and the range of all grenades you throw is doubled.  
**Artillery Expert:** Add \+3 gun slots, and you may now take the Change Weapons Operation at will on your turn without having to spend a Tertiary Operation.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+25 Interaction Points.

Fleet Commander:  
**Jack of All Trades:** Select any two abilities of Commander rank or lower.  
**Diversified Tactics:** Select any ability from any class of Commander rank or lower, excluding Starting Abilities.  
**Berserker:** When you fall below half base health, you take half damage (rounded down) from all attacks. Additionally, all melee attacks deal twice the attack’s base amount of damage dice.

Hyper-Lethal Vector  
**Landmine:** You may spend an hour to create up to two landmines a foot across and a foot wide. These mines can be detonated from up to 5 miles away, or when triggered by at least five pounds of pressure. This mine can be attached to any surface or buried underground, taking five extra pounds of pressure to detonate for each foot underground it is. Any creature who steps on the landmine instantly takes 28 (5d10) explosive damage with no dodge, and all creatures within 20 feet must make a Dodge DC 80 or take full damage and be exposed to the Fallen effect, but only takes half damage (rounded down) on a success. The landmine can also be thrown up to 20 feet if so chosen. It takes a Primary Operation to detonate a landmine.  
**Explosive Confidence:** As a Primary Operation once per downtime your explosive antics inspire your companions. Any allies, including you, within 30 feet of you may use a grenade as a Secondary Operation, and gain any abilities related to explosive damage and weapons that you have. This aura lasts for a minute.

## Engineer

While the battle rages on, a Spartan on the backlines works on a mechanical appliance that resembles a turret. After only a few minutes, the turret is online, and opens fire on the Covenant forces. She eliminates the last few grunts with her dual SMGs, claiming the battle as a UNSC victory. The engineer is a highly-intelligent support unit who relies on an automated combat turret in tight situations.

**Statistics:**  
Health: 45  
Shields: 55  
Health per rank up: 6 (1d10)  
Speed: 30 feet  
Size: Medium  
Recommended Starting Weaponry: Two SMGs  
Superiorities: Tech, Handling  
Expertises: Crafting, Firepower  
Gun Carrying Capacity: You have 3 gun slots  
Grenade Capacity: You have 6 grenade slots

**Starting Ability:** *Turret.* As a Primary Operation you can deploy a chaingun turret anywhere within 5 feet that operates on its own, taking its turn directly after yours. This turret has 75 health with a dodge penalty of \-30. As a Primary Operation you may quickly repair your turret by making a Crafting interaction with a DC equal to the total amount of health lost by the turret, restoring half of the turret’s lost health on a success (rounded down), provided you are within 5 feet of your turret. When it is not in use, it regains 5 health per minute. If the turret reaches 0 health, you must spend an uninterrupted hour to repair the turret, restoring it to maximum health, or crafting a new one if it was lost. You may have no more than 1 turret at a time. While within 5 feet of the turret, you may deactivate and store the turret as a Secondary Operation, placing it on the Spartan’s back where it takes up no inventory space.

2nd Lieutenant:   
**Hearty:** Add \+8 to your base health.  
**Improved Shields:** Add \+5 to your base shields.  
**Extended Grenade Belt**: Add \+1 grenade slot.  
**Extended Hip Holster:** Add \+1 gun slot.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+5 Interaction Points.

1st Lieutenant:  
**Agile:** Add \+5 to all dodges.  
**Medic:** During a downtime, you can create up to 3 medpacs.  
**Disable:** As a Secondary Operation you can disable any simple electronic device that you could normally influence with the Tech interaction within 20 feet of you for up to 1 minute. 

Captain:   
**Master Craftsman:** You may spend 10 minutes to create a machine that adds \+20 to a single type of interaction while in your possession. You may only have one of these machines active at one time.   
**Ammo Dispensary:** You may spend 10 uninterrupted minutes to craft up to 5 Ammo Die for any weapon. These do not all have to be for the same weapon, but they cannot exceed the maximum ammo die allowed for by the weapon.  
**Combat Medicine**: 3 times per downtime, you may spend a Secondary Operation to grant a creature within 5 feet of you up to \+20 health. 

Major:  
**Hearty:** Add \+13 to your base health.  
**Improved Shields:** Add \+8 to your base shields.  
**Extended Grenade Belt:** Add \+1 grenade slot.  
**Extended Hip Holster:** Add \+1 gun slot.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+10 Interaction Points.

Lieutenant Colonel:   
**Anti-Gravity Armor:** Once per day you can activate a series of anti-gravity thrusters for up to 10 minutes. These thrusters limit your speed to your base speed minus 5, however you can now walk on any surface, such as walls and ceilings. Additionally, difficult terrain does not limit your movement speed and you cannot take fall damage while this is active.  
**Thermal Imaging Goggles:** Twice per downtime, for a minute each, you can activate thermal imaging goggles in your helmet that allow you to see and locate the thermal imaging of any creature within 60 feet, penetrating only through light underbrush and similar obstructions. These goggles allow you to ignore any penalties imposed by fighting in darkness. You can also read the current health and strength of the shields on up to 5 creatures.  
**Doctor:** When using a medpac, the health regained is now equal to the amount rolled on a Medicinal interaction without halving it, adding all bonuses.

Colonel Major:  
**Weapon Creation:** You can spend an uninterrupted hour to create up to 3 gun slots worth of UNSC weaponry. These weapons can be changed out any time you spend an hour doing so. **Improved Turret:** When you deploy your turret, you may now choose whether it takes the form of a chaingun, gauss, or rocket turret. The chosen type can be changed when you next deploy your turret. In addition, your turret now has 100 base health.   
**Shoulder Turret:** As a Secondary Operation, you may activate a shoulder-mounted turret. As a Tertiary Operation, you may have the turret make up to 2 attacks. The turret has Dodge DC 60, and deals 9 (2d8)  kinetic damage on a hit. This turret lasts for up to a minute and can be ended early as a Tertiary Operation. This can be done up to twice per downtime.

Field Marshal:  
**Hearty:** Add \+22 to base health.  
**Improved Shields:** Add \+18 to base shields.  
**Extended Grenade Belt:** Add \+2 grenade slots.  
**Extended Hip Holster:** Add \+2 gun slots.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+15 Interaction Points.

Lieutenant General:  
**Tripwire:** You have a tripwire that you can place as a Primary Operation, creating a line up to 20 feet long that requires a DC 85 detection check for someone who isn’t aware of its presence to find. Anyone who walks through it must make a DC 80 dodge or be exposed to the fallen effect.  
**Immunity to Effects:** As a Tertiary Operation you may cleanse an ally within 30 feet of 1 effect other than wounded.  
**Tactical Advantage:** As a Reactive Operation, when you or an ally within 30 feet of you makes a dodge you may add a \+20 to the dodge. You must do this before you know the result of the dodge.

General Major:  
**Vehicle Rewire:** Twice per downtime, you can use Primary Operation to rewire a vehicle's hardware to rig it to explode at a time of your choosing. The vehicle must be within 5 feet, but after rewiring the vehicle, you may choose to detonate it anytime between 1-5 rounds after rewiring it. Until the designated time of explosion, the vehicle operates as normal.   
**Attachment Crafting:** Your expertise in engineering lets you create up to 5 gun attachment slots. To do so you must spend an hour crafting per slot. Slots are determined as follows:

- Tier I: 1 slot  
- Tier II: 2 slots  
- Tier III: 3 slots  
- Tier IV: 4 slots  
- Tier V: 5 slots

If you wish to change the attachments you have crafted, you must spend the necessary amount of time to create a new attachment and dismantle the previous attachments.  
**Autosentry:** As a Primary Operation you can create an autosentry using this ability. This autosentry stays in place for up to four rounds unless it is destroyed or you take a Tertiary Operation to dismiss it. The autosentry takes its turn directly after your own. You may deploy up to 3 autosentries per downtime.

Autosentry  
Health: 50  
Damage: 3d10  
Dodge: DC 65  
Size: N/A  
Type: Semiautomatic  
Maximum Ammo Storage: N/A  
Shots per Magazine: N/A  
Attacks: 2  
Dual-Wield: N/A  
Precision Weapon: No  
Range: 30 feet

**Special Abilities:** N/A

Commander:  
**Heart of a Lion:** Add \+31 to base health, and at the start of each of your turns you regain 5 health as long as you are conscious.  
**Shield of the People:** Add \+26 to your base shields, and once per downtime, you can bring yourself back to full shields as a Tertiary Operation.  
**Loose Cannon:** Add \+3 grenade slots, and the range of all grenades you throw is doubled..  
**Artillery Expert:** Add \+3 gun slots, and you may now take the Change Weapons Operation at will on your turn without having to spend a Tertiary Operation.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+25 Interaction Points.

Fleet Commander:  
**Jack of All Trades:** Select any two abilities of Commander rank or lower.  
**Diversified Tactics:** Select any ability from any class of Commander rank or lower, excluding Starting Abilities.  
**Retaliatory Surge:** As a Reactive Operation, after all of your shield health has been depleted, you release a surge of energy centered around yourself. Any target of your choice within 20 feet must succeed on a DC 85 dodge or take 28 (5d10) shock damage (DC 65 Fortitude).

Hyper-Lethal Vector:  
**Electrocution Pods:** You have 5 electrocution pods that can be used once each per downtime. They can be placed or thrown as no Operation and detonated as a Secondary Operation. Each pod is only a few inches wide and when detonated emits an electric charge targeting up to 5 creatures of the player’s choice within 10 feet of the pod. Each targeted creature must make a DC 80 dodge or take 18 (4d8) damage shock damage (DC 60 Fortitude) and be stunned until the end of your next turn. You cannot detonate more than 1 pod per turn.   
**Damage Absorption Suit Upgrade:** You have a module within your armor that allows you to absorb up to 200 points of damage. When you make a dodge (against an attack dealing damage) that exceeds the Dodge DC by 15 or more, you may absorb the damage that would have been dealt to you. The extra damage acts as a pool that you can draw on, and you may add a chosen amount of damage from this pool to the damage dealt by an attack you make, with the extra damage becoming the same damage type as is dealt by the attack. 

## 

## Heavy 

A massive warrior comes barreling through his foes, with a chaingun in hand. His enemies cower before him as he weathers all of their attacks, leaving a trail of dead Covenant in his wake. This is the heavy, a class known to be able to withstand enormous amounts of damage while annihilating all enemies in their path with a massive detached turret.

**Statistics:**  
Health: 60  
Shields: 75  
Health per rank up: 7 (1d12)  
Speed: 20 feet  
Size: Medium  
Recommended Starting Weaponry: Chaingun  
Superiorities: Firepower, Charisma  
Expertises: Fortitude, Lifting  
Gun Carrying Capacity: You have 5 gun slots  
Grenade Capacity: You have 8 grenade slots

**Starting Ability:** *Charge:* Twice per downtime, as a Secondary Operation and Tertiary Operation you can choose to charge 1 target. When you charge you gain an additional 10 feet of movement speed. You then must spend at least 10 feet of movement moving toward an enemy, but do not provoke any chance attacks. If you end your movement within 5 feet of a target, the target must then make a Dodge DC 60 or take 28 (8d6) kinetic damage and be exposed to the Fallen effect. 

2nd Lieutenant:  
**Hearty:** Add \+10 to your base health.  
**Improved Shields:** Add \+7 to your base shields.  
**Extended Grenade Belt**: Add \+1 grenade slot.  
**Extended Hip Holster:** Add \+1 gun slot.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+5 Interaction Points.

1st Lieutenant:  
**Bulky:** When enemies try to move you against your will, you gain a \+20 to dodges and contests to resist being moved.  
**Fortitude:** Twice per downtime, as a Reactive Operation, when you take damage, you may roll a d20 and reduce the damage taken by that amount.   
**Vigorous:** You may add \+20 to any lifting interactions you make.

Captain:  
**Large Weapons Expert:** When using a weapon of size large or larger, add an extra \+1 damage die.  
**Interpose:** As a reactionary Operation, you may interpose yourself between an ally and any single attack targeting that ally provided you are within 5 feet of your ally, with you taking the full damage of the attack and the ally taking no damage as a result. If the ally was the target for a radius-based attack, you become the target instead.  
**Strong:** You ignore movement penalties made by carrying turrets and may use all combat maneuvers while carrying a turret.

Major:  
**Hearty:** Add \+20 to your base health.  
**Improved Shields:** Add \+12 to your base shields.  
**Extended Grenade Belt:** Add \+1 grenade slot.  
**Extended Hip Holster:** Add \+1 gun slot.  
**Interaction Points:** You gain \+10 Interaction Points.

Lieutenant Colonel:  
**Repel:** As a reactionary Operation once every two turns, you may repel a single attack from a medium or smaller weapon that targets you or anything within 5 feet of you. The attacking creature then becomes the target of the attack but that attack’s Dodge DC is decreased by \-15.  
**Portable Energy Shield:** You gain an additional 80 shields, however these shields do not affect your total shield health or the amount of shields regenerated per turn of not taking damage. Instead, these additional shields generate a portable energy shield emanating around you. If the energy shield has between 1 and 30 shields, it grants Weak cover, if it has between 31 and 60 shields it grants Average cover, and if it has between 61 and 80 shields it grants Sturdy cover. If an attack would otherwise hit but is dodged as a result of the bonus provided from the portable energy shield’s cover, the shield takes the full damage of the attack. As a Secondary Operation, you can place this cover down anywhere within 5 feet. When deployed in this way it provides cover in a 15 foot line reaching 10 feet high. Any creatures behind this cover gain its benefits and can make weapon attacks through the shields with no penalty. As a Tertiary Operation, you may also pick the portable energy shield back up.  
**Anti-Gravity Armor:** Once per day, expending no Operations, you can activate a series of anti-gravity thrusters for up to ten minutes. These thrusters limit your speed to your base speed minus 5, however you can now walk on any surface, such as walls and ceilings. Additionally, difficult terrain does not limit your movement speed and you cannot take fall damage while this is active.

Colonel Major:
